  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_26399239-8cc0-4baa-88e1-10d4e26dfed9'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer9140984854009395043">Twelve-year-old Mosca Mye hasn't got much. Her cruel uncle keeps her locked up in his mill, and her only friend is her pet goose, Saracen, who'll bite anything that crosses his path.   <span id="freeText9140984854009395043" style="display:none">Twelve-year-old Mosca Mye hasn't got much. Her cruel uncle keeps her locked up in his mill, and her only friend is her pet goose, Saracen, who'll bite anything that crosses his path. But she does have one small, rare thing: the ability to read. She doesn't know it yet, but in a world where books are dangerous things, this gift will change her life.<br /><br />Enter Eponymous Clent, a smooth-talking con man who seems to love words nearly as much as Mosca herself. Soon Mosca and Clent are living a life of deceit and danger -- discovering secret societies, following shady characters onto floating coffeehouses, and entangling themselves with crazed dukes and double-crossing racketeers. It would be exactly the kind of tale Mosca has always longed to take part in, until she learns that her one true love -- words -- may be the death of her.<br /><br />"Fly by Night" is astonishingly original, a grand feat of the imagination from a masterful new storyteller.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Then this book will be perfect for them. It's clever, entertaining and appropriate for that age. <br/><br/>PS In case you're religious : It's got some ..how sho<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Then this book will be perfect for them. It's clever, entertaining and appropriate for that age. <br /><br />PS In case you're religious : It's got some ..how should I phrase this.. I've heard it described as..*cough* as a leaning towards *cough* atheist propaganda. But the references, in my opinion, towards the end are very subtle so there really shouldn't be any problem at all. I thought I'd mention it just in case.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

    <a title="Adam Boisvert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/359900-adam-boisvert"><img alt="Adam Boisvert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251430225p2/359900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6194363?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Adam Boisvert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Adam Boisvert" href="/user/show/359900-adam-boisvert">Adam Boisvert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6194363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3930655796570193152">In the back of Fly By Night, Frances Hardinge gives us the following warning: "This is not a historical novel. It is a yarn. Although the Realm is based roughly on England at the start of the eighteenth century, I have taken appalling liberties with historical authenticity and, when I felt like it, the laws of physics."<br/><br/>What she fails to mention is that it's a rollicking good yarn. It follows the adventures (and mis-adventures) of Mosca Mye. Her problem is she loves words of all shapes and sizes </span>
  <span id="freeText3930655796570193152" style="display:none">In the back of Fly By Night, Frances Hardinge gives us the following warning: "This is not a historical novel. It is a yarn. Although the Realm is based roughly on England at the start of the eighteenth century, I have taken appalling liberties with historical authenticity and, when I felt like it, the laws of physics."<br /><br />What she fails to mention is that it's a rollicking good yarn. It follows the adventures (and mis-adventures) of Mosca Mye. Her problem is she loves words of all shapes and sizes (her father broke convention and taught her to read before he conventionally died) but she lives in a world where most folks fear education and distrust any sort of writing. In trying to better herself and broaden her horizons she encounters a variety of colourful characters, from con men to tradesmen, dutchesses to revolutionaries. Written by, for, and about bibliophiles; Fly By Night is ultimately a story about the power of words, and whether this power should be feared or embraced.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3930655796570193152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_23647637" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/23647637" />
    <a title="Lucy " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45923-lucy"><img alt="Lucy " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300985055p2/45923.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/23647637?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy " href="/user/show/45923-lucy">Lucy </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">rena p.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=kidlit">kidlit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=books-that-deserve-six-stars">books-that-deserve-six-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23647637" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7388487599885284632">Fly By Night opens with a short history of The Fractured Realm, and things look grim indeed. A history peppered with monarchs and parliament, guild wars and religious inquisitions, and a holy terror of the dangers of the written word are the backdrop for this story. <br/><br/>Mosca Mye, orphaned, black-eyed and stubborn and addicted to the written word, burns down her uncle’s mill (accidentally,) releases a con man from the stocks (on purpose,) and flees town with only her homicidal and loyal goose Sarace</span>
  <span id="freeText7388487599885284632" style="display:none">Fly By Night opens with a short history of The Fractured Realm, and things look grim indeed. A history peppered with monarchs and parliament, guild wars and religious inquisitions, and a holy terror of the dangers of the written word are the backdrop for this story. <br /><br />Mosca Mye, orphaned, black-eyed and stubborn and addicted to the written word, burns down her uncle’s mill (accidentally,) releases a con man from the stocks (on purpose,) and flees town with only her homicidal and loyal goose Saracen as a companion. And thus begins Mosca’s adventure in a city that is a political hotbed of unrest, where people are rarely what they seem and loyalties may change at the drop of a hat. Mosca only wants to find her place and follow her love of the written word, but she will soon find herself a pawn in a political intrigue that has many sides. Only her fierce ingenuity (and Saracen’s loyalty) will be able to help her make it out alive.<br /><br />This is one of those brilliant books with a million details and descriptions and characters, but all of them are interesting and important and colorful and worth reading about. The Fractured Realm has one of the most interesting political and religious histories that I have seen in children’s literature – or any literature – in quite a while. It is quite an ambitious feat, and Hardinge pulls it off with aplomb. Hardinge’s character descriptions are short but paint the picture. (One example: “The captain was a grim-smiling river-king named Partridge. There was something crooked in the make of his right wrist, as if it had been broken and never quite healed, and something crooked in the corner of his smile, as if that too had been broken and put back together slightly wrong.”) And lest you think the details superfluous, they are always important and relevant and interesting. I daresay there is not one inch of superfluous material in this brilliant story. And Mosca is an irrepressibly likeable heroine who learns early on how to lie convincingly and how to stay afloat and try to do the right thing. She is clever and interesting and smart and a lot of fun, and I would happily read more about Mosca and her homicidal Saracen. It goes without saying (but I will say it anyway) that this book is highly, highly recommended for anyone who likes interesting characters, political and religious unrest done well, compelling stories and/or good writing. Which is to say, everyone.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7388487599885284632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2814153754" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2814153754" />
    <a title="Bradley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley"><img alt="Bradley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508811508p2/4213258.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2814153754?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2019-shelf">2019-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2814153754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9752545227282697899">I've read a number of book-centric books over the years and quite a few of them are YA. Some hit you over the head with the book and others are subtle enough to flow right over you and sneak up and bite you in the behind.<br/><br/>This one is the latter kind.<br/><br/>Sure, the power of words is all over the place, but where I like it most is in Hardinge's worldbuilding. The history of this place is not only fascinating and rough, but clever and multilayered. I get the impression we're in an early English period ri</span>
  <span id="freeText9752545227282697899" style="display:none">I've read a number of book-centric books over the years and quite a few of them are YA. Some hit you over the head with the book and others are subtle enough to flow right over you and sneak up and bite you in the behind.<br /><br />This one is the latter kind.<br /><br />Sure, the power of words is all over the place, but where I like it most is in Hardinge's worldbuilding. The history of this place is not only fascinating and rough, but clever and multilayered. I get the impression we're in an early English period right after the printing press came out. But unlike that period, books soon became anathema. Like religious persecution, even. <br /><br />Of course, that makes our heroes and villains well-learned action types falling in with thieves and revolutionaries, and that's just plain fun. <br /><br />So why did I give this four stars rather than five? Because some of the text is a bit dense and the flow wasn't perfect. But I LOVED the world and had a pretty good time with the characters. And the God Goose. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9752545227282697899" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_364366020" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/364366020" />
    <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers"><img alt="TheBookSmugglers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316717753p2/1223249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/364366020?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheBookSmugglers" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers">TheBookSmugglers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer364366020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8743156495870772634">Original review posted on <a href='http://thebooksmugglers.com/2012/07/book-review-fly-by-night-by-frances-hardinge.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Book Smugglers</a><br/><br/>I am overcome with Imperious Feelings demanding that I find the Right Words to write this review. Fly By Night is Absurdly Brilliant. This is not an overstatement.<br/><br/>How else could I possibly qualify a book that features a main character named Mosca1 Mye whose love for words is both impetus and trademark? Whose love for words is the driving force toward a life of High Adventure in the company of a smooth-talking charlatan named Eponymous Clent and a murde</span>
  <span id="freeText8743156495870772634" style="display:none">Original review posted on <a href="http://thebooksmugglers.com/2012/07/book-review-fly-by-night-by-frances-hardinge.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Smugglers</a><br /><br />I am overcome with Imperious Feelings demanding that I find the Right Words to write this review. Fly By Night is Absurdly Brilliant. This is not an overstatement.<br /><br />How else could I possibly qualify a book that features a main character named Mosca1 Mye whose love for words is both impetus and trademark? Whose love for words is the driving force toward a life of High Adventure in the company of a smooth-talking charlatan named Eponymous Clent and a murderous pet Goose named Saracen? Whose journey takes her through completely unpredictable twists and turns in a political game where no one knows who is ally or foe?<br /><br />If not brilliant, what other word could I possibly use to describe a book that is defined by original, unusual worldbuilding as well as Impressive Intellectual Sharpness?<br /><br />With regards to the former: Fly By Night is set in an alternate 18th Century (but not quite) where years ago, after getting rid of its monarchy, the Fractured Realm plunged into a gruesome Civil War when Birdcatchers – a radical religious movement – came to power. Ten years after all Birdcatchers have been killed (or have they?), the Realm is ran by different Guilds of Tradesmen. The Guilds’ power have been growing exponentially, especially that of the Stationers Guild (who control all printing materials, anything without their seal is deemed illegal) ; the Locksmiths Guild (who have the keys to every door) ; and the Watermen Guild (who control all movement along the river). The power balance is precariously held together by a truce between all Guilds and even one small wrong move could start a whole new war. Mosca and Clent (and Saracen) find themselves in the middle of this complex game of power which is complicated by a Duke who is slowly going mad and whose sister has Ideas of Her Own. Not to mention the emergence of an illegal printing press that has been spreading Illegal Radical Words all over the Realm.<br /><br />The latter comes from the fact that this is a book with a main character who loves words in a world that fears them. Being a book about words – their importance, their potential, their beauty – one of the most brilliant things about it is how the author brandishes her words like Weapons of Mass Construction.<br /><br />From the Thought Provoking:<br /><br /> <i>Brand a man as a thief and no one will ever hire him for honest labor – he will be a hardened robber within weeks. The brand does not reveal a person’s nature, it shapes it.</i><br /><br />Via the Utterly Hilarious:<br /><br /> <i>(…)Mosca and Saracen shared, if not a friendship, at least the solidarity of the generally despised.</i><br /><br />All the way to the Extremely Acute:<br /><br /> <i> ‘Where is your sense of patriotism?’<br /><br /> ‘I kept it hid away safe, along with my sense of trust, Mr Clent. I don’t use ‘em much in case they get scratched.’</i><br /><br />And the Plain Beautiful:<br /><br /> <i> ‘But in the name of the most holy, Mosca, of all the people you could have taken up with, why Eponymous Clent?’<br /><br /> Because I’d been hoarding words for years, buying them from peddlers and carving them secretly on to bits of bark so I wouldn’t forget them, and then he turned up using words like ‘epiphany’ and ‘amaranth’. Because I heard him talking in the marketplace, laying out sentences like a merchant rolling out rich silks. Because he made words and ideas dance like flames and something that was damp and dying came alive in my mind, the way it hadn’t since they burned my father’s books. Because he walked into Chough with stories from exciting places tangled around him like maypole streamers…<br /><br /> Mosca shrugged.<br /><br /> ‘He’s got a way with words.’</i><br /><br />Fly By Night is a book that provokes, incites and invites the reader to participate in a wordily love-fest. Granted that at times, this comes across as slightly heavy-handed especially towards the ending but this was simply not enough to make any damage to the immense love I feel for this book.<br /><br />But that is not all! For Fly By Night is also Coming of Age of the Highest Quality. Mosca’s journey is superbly executed by exploring her loneliness, her perceived uniqueness (which is not true at all, given the truths that she unveils) as well as the connections she forms with other people (especially the Cakes. How could I not love the Cakes?). Her arc has moments of Utter Despair, Sad Mistakes as well as Great Bravery.<br /><br />Most of all, I loved the development of the relationship with Clent and I loved the bond they formed over a shared loved for words (for better or worse). Take this incredible moment where they have a fight:<br /><br /> <i>Mosca’s opening offer was a number of cant words she had heard peddlers use, words for the drool hanging from a dog’s jaw, words for the greenish sheen on a mouldering strip of bacon.<br /> Eponymous Clent responded with some choice descriptions of ungrateful and treacherous women culled from ballad and classic myth.<br /> Mosca countered with some from her secret hoard of hidden words, the terms used by smugglers for tell-alls, and soldiers’ words for the worst kind of keyhole-stooping spy.<br /> Clent answered with crushing and high-sounding examples from the best essays on the natural depravity of unguided youth.</i><br /><br />Isn’t this Staggering Good Writing?<br /><br />I had a lot of fun reading Fly By Night and as you can probably see, a lot of fun writing this review too. I freaking love when that happens, those are the best kind of books. Fly By Night is a Totally Awesome Book and I already got the sequel because one is not enough for me: just like Mosca, I too, want more story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8743156495870772634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1836077-lightreads?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer644283463" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11754098236238563969">Frances Hardinge understands all those important rules of storycraft like 'the true tension is internal,' and 'you don't have to be good to be relatable,' and 'if you put a loaded goose on the mantelpiece in act I, you have to fire it by act V.'<br/><br/>Ung, so good. So so good. This was her first published novel, and it's true, it doesn't have the tautness and precision of her later <i>The Lost Conspiracy</i>. But this is also a weird and wonderful book. It's young adult fantasy about a twelve-year-old girl wh</span>
  <span id="freeText11754098236238563969" style="display:none">Frances Hardinge understands all those important rules of storycraft like 'the true tension is internal,' and 'you don't have to be good to be relatable,' and 'if you put a loaded goose on the mantelpiece in act I, you have to fire it by act V.'<br /><br />Ung, so good. So so good. This was her first published novel, and it's true, it doesn't have the tautness and precision of her later <i>The Lost Conspiracy</i>. But this is also a weird and wonderful book. It's young adult fantasy about a twelve-year-old girl who burns down her uncle's sawmill and blackmails her way out of her tiny town with a confidence man and her homicidal goose companion (though, really, given geese, that's redundant, I could just say "her goose companion.") This book kept shifting under my feet. First it was blackhearted bickering roadtrip funtimes, and then it was fantasy spy funtimes, and then it was about revolutions, and then it was about illegal printing presses, and then it was about trust and ferocity and betrayal and growing a conscience and so many other things all at once that I can't remember them all.<br /><br />But mostly it's about Mosca, who is twelve and messed up and literate but undereducated and curious and coldhearted. And I loved her so much. Here she is, judge for yourself:<br /><br />""Sacred just means something you're not meant to think about properly, and you should never stop thinking. Show me something I can kick, and hit with rocks, and set fire to, and leave out in the rain, and think about. And if it's still standing after all that, then maybe, just maybe, I'll start to believe in it, but not till then.""<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11754098236238563969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2841988909?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2841988909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7983033383139695330">This is my third book by this author and the first she ever published. Sadly, it shows.<br/><br/>The story is that of a world where books have become forbidden. Into this world a girl is born with the unusual name of Mosca. The girl is smart and inquisitive and loves learning about words. As is only natural for a story like this, personal disaster strikes and she is forced to flee her home together with her gander (the best character here if you ask me). She meets a lot of people, from vagabonds to thieve</span>
  <span id="freeText7983033383139695330" style="display:none">This is my third book by this author and the first she ever published. Sadly, it shows.<br /><br />The story is that of a world where books have become forbidden. Into this world a girl is born with the unusual name of Mosca. The girl is smart and inquisitive and loves learning about words. As is only natural for a story like this, personal disaster strikes and she is forced to flee her home together with her gander (the best character here if you ask me). She meets a lot of people, from vagabonds to thieves to royalty to tyrants and many more.<br />A revolution in this strange and yet familiar world is inevitable and of course Mosca is at the center of it all.<br /><br />I really liked the premise of this story that is set in a world where words have so much power. And I liked the author's worldbuilding as much as her own way with words. However, the story itself was dragging on and on and on and just couldn't grab me. In the end, a good idea and nice prose turned out not to be enough for me, sadly.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong, the story is multilayered, the characters show potential. So it wasn't actually bad (see my rating). However, the characters never truly reached their full potential and the twists were ... not really twist-y for me but rather predictable.<br /><br />Sometimes you just don't click with a story and this was such a moment for me. I loved her other two books and am looking forward to the new one coming out shortly, but this was kind of a let-down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7983033383139695330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1014437377820882826"><i>"Where is your sense of patriotism?"<br/>"I keep it hid away safe, along with my sense of trust, Mr Clent. I don't use 'em much in case they get scratched."</i><br/><br/>Frances Hardinge can certainly turn a wonderful phrase. Her words skip and giggle and gleam, at once sly and coy. Characters are never simply "brown haired" or "blue eyed" but rather given descriptions such as <i>"The little man's mouth was a small, bitter V-shape, and seemed designed to say small, bitter things."</i><br/><br/>Unfortunately, in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/710437.Fly_by_Night__Fly_By_Night___1_' title='Fly by Night (Fly By Night, #1) by Frances Hardinge' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fly by Night</a>, the p</span>
  <span id="freeText1014437377820882826" style="display:none"><i>"Where is your sense of patriotism?"<br />"I keep it hid away safe, along with my sense of trust, Mr Clent. I don't use 'em much in case they get scratched."</i><br /><br />Frances Hardinge can certainly turn a wonderful phrase. Her words skip and giggle and gleam, at once sly and coy. Characters are never simply "brown haired" or "blue eyed" but rather given descriptions such as <i>"The little man's mouth was a small, bitter V-shape, and seemed designed to say small, bitter things."</i><br /><br />Unfortunately, in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/710437.Fly_by_Night__Fly_By_Night___1_" title="Fly by Night (Fly By Night, #1) by Frances Hardinge" rel="nofollow noopener">Fly by Night</a>, the plot leaps about as wildly as the words - and this is no longer such a compliment. Characters are trusted and not trusted and trusted again and everyone is constantly on different sides, motives changing so often it almost gives you whiplash to read about. Later books weave their pieces together far better than here.</span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/11313923?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="wittierninja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="wittierninja" href="/user/show/313335-wittierninja">wittierninja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who liked Inkheart by Cornelia Funke or The Never-Ending Story</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/313335-wittierninja?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer11313923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1771833491019279809">This is truly a book about readers, for readers. I know that the plot is not unfamiliar to many of you: lonely girl or boy, spends more time with books than with people because books are friendlier, kinder, less cruel. And then something magical happens, blah blah blah. <i>Fly by Night</i> is a little different in that instead of exploring the power of books to a child, it delves into the strength of words and names, and how both affect the world and how they determine the kind of person you become. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText1771833491019279809" style="display:none">This is truly a book about readers, for readers. I know that the plot is not unfamiliar to many of you: lonely girl or boy, spends more time with books than with people because books are friendlier, kinder, less cruel. And then something magical happens, blah blah blah. <i>Fly by Night</i> is a little different in that instead of exploring the power of books to a child, it delves into the strength of words and names, and how both affect the world and how they determine the kind of person you become. The writing is smooth, and I had, at first, thought it was going to be those types of books that looks great (spot lam! cool jacket art! rough edges!) but is poorly written. I am happy to say I was pleasantly surprised. If you're looking for something easy to read, easy to enjoy, and easy to lose yourself into, then I'd definitely encourage you try this.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2574920" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2574920" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/163929-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1259986339p2/163929.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2574920?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/163929-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/163929-ashley?shelf=juvenilefantasy">juvenilefantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2574920" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9957021177119416540">This is probably the best example of what I call "not-quite-fantasy" that I've read since Lloyd Alexander's The Kestral. While it takes place in a fictional country loosely based on seventeenth century England, there is no magic in this story, except for the elusive magic of words which the author both idolizes and exhibits in her own gorgeous prose. The young protagonist makes her way through a complex and realistically imagined world complete with an elaborate social structure, religion and hi</span>
  <span id="freeText9957021177119416540" style="display:none">This is probably the best example of what I call "not-quite-fantasy" that I've read since Lloyd Alexander's The Kestral. While it takes place in a fictional country loosely based on seventeenth century England, there is no magic in this story, except for the elusive magic of words which the author both idolizes and exhibits in her own gorgeous prose. The young protagonist makes her way through a complex and realistically imagined world complete with an elaborate social structure, religion and history. She struggles convincingly, as so many young adults do, with the question of what to believe and who to trust. I could go on and on about memorable characters, a touch of dark humor, and the author's talent for savoring the absurd. But never mind; just read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9957021177119416540" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_56169494" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/56169494" />
    <a title="Anna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/402878-anna"><img alt="Anna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452859934p2/402878.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/56169494?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna" href="/user/show/402878-anna">Anna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer56169494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8093549333805582268">I thought that this book was great. It had an intriguing plot line, plenty of twists and turns, and each chapter was a different letter of the alphabet (A Is For Arsony, etc.). HOWEVER, I was disappointed with the ending. Rather than subtly make a point and then end the story, the author got incredibly PREACHY. I think the point could have been made succintly and then the story could have cheerfully trotted along to it's conclusion. Instead, the author went on and on. Her point wasn't bad (basic</span>
  <span id="freeText8093549333805582268" style="display:none">I thought that this book was great. It had an intriguing plot line, plenty of twists and turns, and each chapter was a different letter of the alphabet (A Is For Arsony, etc.). HOWEVER, I was disappointed with the ending. Rather than subtly make a point and then end the story, the author got incredibly PREACHY. I think the point could have been made succintly and then the story could have cheerfully trotted along to it's conclusion. Instead, the author went on and on. Her point wasn't bad (basically, it's wrong to force people to believe something and kill them if they won't), but she ruined the point by making it too clear. Also, the cover says "Imagine a world in which all books are BANNED!", which is fairly inaccurate. Not ALL books are banned, just the unapproved ones. Is there a big heap o' censorship going on in this story? Yes. Are ALL books banned? No.<br />So, good story. Disappointingly preachy, though.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8093549333805582268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_33622460" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33622460" />
    <a title="Mika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/917083-mika"><img alt="Mika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249542020p2/917083.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33622460?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mika" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mika" href="/user/show/917083-mika">Mika</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33622460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer206236804984168052">As I sat down to write this post, I thought, “You know, the title really doesn’t make any sense. It has nothing to do with the book at all.” Oh my, I am losing it. I somehow failed to make the connection between the main character’s name, Mosca (in honor of the day she was born on - sacred to Goodman Palpitattle, He Who Keeps Flies out of Jams and Butter Churns), and the double meaning of the word fly. Sheesh.<br/><br/>The plot was extremely unique. In whatever world this takes place in (one thing I can h</span>
  <span id="freeText206236804984168052" style="display:none">As I sat down to write this post, I thought, “You know, the title really doesn’t make any sense. It has nothing to do with the book at all.” Oh my, I am losing it. I somehow failed to make the connection between the main character’s name, Mosca (in honor of the day she was born on - sacred to Goodman Palpitattle, He Who Keeps Flies out of Jams and Butter Churns), and the double meaning of the word fly. Sheesh.<br /><br />The plot was extremely unique. In whatever world this takes place in (one thing I can hardly ever be bothered to pay attention to), there was originally a monarchy; several deaths lead to an argument over succession; a parliament was established, but the real force behind the realm - and the glue that held it together - was the guilds. Each has its own responsibilities and jurisdictions. Eventually it is decided that a parliamentary committee will decide on the best monarch to rule; meanwhile, the residents of the realm are free to support their favored monarch, as well as the Beloved (basically a Saint) that suits them best. There is a Beloved for each day and each night of the year, so babies are named for the Beloved on whose day or night they are born.<br /><br />Mosca is a young girl who was taught to read by her father before he passed away in a remote village, where he moved when he was exiled (although we don’t learn why until later) many years before. She escapes the village and moves on to bigger, better, and more troublesome things.<br /><br />The big question: did I see the plot twists coming? Heavens no, but I was really trying this time. I picked up on what clues I could, yet was completely blindsided by the sudden turn of events. The author did a great job balancing foreshadowing and real surprises. It was a quick, easy read, and as I said, the plot was fantastic. I actually grabbed the book at the library because it was thick and had a cool cover…luckily I was not disappointed this time.<br /><br />Hooray for good children’s books!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="206236804984168052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen Healey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen Healey" href="/user/show/347821-karen-healey">Karen Healey</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer61743082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5045684406380956142">A wild delight; a madcap adventure and a fascinating argument for freedom of speech and religion in a fantasy world like a torn and muddied red velvet cape. It's populated with fantastic characters and a plot so twisty and so full of swiftly-changing alliances and factions that Locke Lamora would have trouble untangling it.<br/><br/>Highly, highly recommended.<br/><br/>(Also, one of the main characters is named EPONYMOUS CLENT. I don't believe there's been a more perfectly-named character in the history of ever.)<br/><br/><br/>Th</span>
  <span id="freeText5045684406380956142" style="display:none">A wild delight; a madcap adventure and a fascinating argument for freedom of speech and religion in a fantasy world like a torn and muddied red velvet cape. It's populated with fantastic characters and a plot so twisty and so full of swiftly-changing alliances and factions that Locke Lamora would have trouble untangling it.<br /><br />Highly, highly recommended.<br /><br />(Also, one of the main characters is named EPONYMOUS CLENT. I don't believe there's been a more perfectly-named character in the history of ever.)<br /><br /><br />Things I didn't like:<br /><br />- I noticed no people of colour, with the possible exception of two "gypsy" girls who appear for a brief scene, and are described as darker than Mosca. The author notes that the book was based roughly on the England of the early eighteenth century, but as she also notes that she has taken "appalling liberties with historical authenticity" *and* the laws of physics, I don't consider this adequate reason for Yet Another White Fantasy World.<br /><br />Things I did like:<br /><br />- EVERYTHING ELSE. It's thoughtful, adventurous, compellingly written with beautiful description and... really, it reminded me most of Diana Wynne Jones, but less talky-directly-to-reader.<br /><br />Lines like this are everywhere: "The waterfall spray beat the leaves with a noise like paper children applauding."<br /><br />&lt;3 &lt;3 &lt;3 &lt;3 &lt;3</span>

It's always delightful to me to watch a character think, and Mosca puzzles out all the intrigues very well. And, she has moments of great valor. And I love all the secondary developments. And I love Mosca's final decisions so much.<br /><br />Read it yourself, and recommend it to every kid from nine through twelve. It has a little something for everyone. <div id="review_150921759" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/150921759" />
    <a title="Hallie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1145657-hallie"><img alt="Hallie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1244842998p2/1145657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150921759?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hallie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hallie" href="/user/show/1145657-hallie">Hallie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1145657-hallie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1145657-hallie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150921759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12908457048339364152">This is a sort of sum of a reading (when it came out, horribly bound paperback - really badly affected readign pleasure) and a listening (audiobook much better, except that Mosca was done as much more street-child than she should have been, given her father and education). While I didn't really feel the love that much on reading, I knew how badly I'd been put off by the binding, and I did indeed really appreciate the love of language that infuses the book through being slowed down to listen. The</span>
  <span id="freeText12908457048339364152" style="display:none">This is a sort of sum of a reading (when it came out, horribly bound paperback - really badly affected readign pleasure) and a listening (audiobook much better, except that Mosca was done as much more street-child than she should have been, given her father and education). While I didn't really feel the love that much on reading, I knew how badly I'd been put off by the binding, and I did indeed really appreciate the love of language that infuses the book through being slowed down to listen. The flip side of that is that it made Mosca's unsympathetic behaviour much harder to take, in slow, painful motion as it was. Understandable that she didn't know if she could trust anyone, of course, but still hard. I'd almost forgotten that part from the reading.<br /><br />I had one -- quibble, disappointment, reservation, whatever. That was that it felt as if Hardinge had made the obvious choice in making the religious system as wonderfully mixed up as the political situation, and then essentially debunking it all. Not that it's a total narrative statement, but it doesn't seem to me to leave a huge amount of room for Mosca's evaluation to be wrong. And having made it so -- goofy (technical theological term there!), it would have been so cool <i>not</i> to have said that the childishness of the saints' followers was indicative of their being wrong to believe at all. One of the things I thought amazing about <i>Gullstruck Island</i> was that Hardinge didn't take the more obvious, easier route of making the Lace the totally 'civilized', noble ones to a totally savage Cavalcaste. I was just kind of sad to see it not working that way in this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12908457048339364152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_157848549" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157848549" />
    <a title="Sesana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana"><img alt="Sesana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413088169p2/5172893.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157848549?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157848549" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15252550020757275417">Ok, I admit it: I basically read this book because of the Brett Helquist art on the cover. I was disappointed to discover that was all he contributed: no interior illustrations. At any rate, the book has a very interesting and unique (to me, at least) premise. It uses the English Revolution as a sort of starting point, the main divergence being that, revolution over, Parliament is given half a dozen or so contenders to become the new monarch and twenty years later, they still haven't decided. In</span>
  <span id="freeText15252550020757275417" style="display:none">Ok, I admit it: I basically read this book because of the Brett Helquist art on the cover. I was disappointed to discover that was all he contributed: no interior illustrations. At any rate, the book has a very interesting and unique (to me, at least) premise. It uses the English Revolution as a sort of starting point, the main divergence being that, revolution over, Parliament is given half a dozen or so contenders to become the new monarch and twenty years later, they still haven't decided. Individual cities are ruled by the trade guilds and by whatever lord holds the territory. Strict censorship is in effect: only books approved by the Stationers Guild can be read. The main character is a girl named Mosca (that's her and her stolen goose, Saracen on the cover). She finds herself mixed up in political machinations in the city of Mandelion. And that's about the best I can do with a fairly complicated plot. I'll probably read more by the author, since it was well-written. And I'll certainly be reading the book she used as reference: 1700: Scenes from London Life. You know, someday. The one issue that I had with it was that Mosca was at least somewhat irritating through most of the book. By the end, I felt like she'd redeemed herself to me, and I ended up liking her more than not. I also wasn't entirely satisfied with how the central mystery was solved. The solution, yes, but not how the characters arrived there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15252550020757275417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_76576778" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76576778" />
    <a title="Lara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/309689-lara"><img alt="Lara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465346130p2/309689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76576778?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lara" href="/user/show/309689-lara">Lara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/309689-lara?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/309689-lara?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76576778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9167904077471847795">I really enjoyed Hardinge's most recent book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6293900.The_Lost_Conspiracy' title='The Lost Conspiracy by Frances Hardinge' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lost Conspiracy</a>, and between that and all the five star reviews for Fly By Night on here, I naturally assumed I'd like this one just as much. But I was wrong. I never really connected with the main character, and then the story itself...just never really interested me (the main point also seemed REALLY heavy handed). And it's very difficult to enjoy a book when you don't care about anybody or anything in it. Another thing: part of what I loved ab</span>
  <span id="freeText9167904077471847795" style="display:none">I really enjoyed Hardinge's most recent book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6293900.The_Lost_Conspiracy" title="The Lost Conspiracy by Frances Hardinge" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lost Conspiracy</a>, and between that and all the five star reviews for Fly By Night on here, I naturally assumed I'd like this one just as much. But I was wrong. I never really connected with the main character, and then the story itself...just never really interested me (the main point also seemed REALLY heavy handed). And it's very difficult to enjoy a book when you don't care about anybody or anything in it. Another thing: part of what I loved about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6293900.The_Lost_Conspiracy" title="The Lost Conspiracy by Frances Hardinge" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lost Conspiracy</a> was that it seemed like EVERY detail brought up somehow came back into the story later on--the plot was so intricately constructed and there were no loose ends or descriptions that didn't matter in some way. But this one felt a lot sloppier and less well constructed. I'm left with the idea that Hardinge has improved much since she published this one, so I'll still give <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2457867.Well_Witched" title="Well Witched by Frances Hardinge" rel="nofollow noopener">Well Witched</a> a try. But now I have much less confindence in that story than I did before I read this one. </span>

<div id="review_443088292" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/443088292" />
    <a title="Nick Fagerlund" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1254063-nick-fagerlund"><img alt="Nick Fagerlund" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1213926376p2/1254063.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/443088292?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick Fagerlund" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick Fagerlund" href="/user/show/1254063-nick-fagerlund">Nick Fagerlund</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer443088292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15934951331668137586">Everybody read this immediately. (Ignore the cover and don't bother reading any promo copy, because the marketing department fixated on the Macguffin and got it two-thirds wrong anyway.)<br/><br/>Mosca, a smart, stubborn, and angry hick who totes a homicidal goose named Saracen, follows a con man named Eponymous Clent to the big city. Espionage, guild warfare, and murder ensue. They accidentally turn some poor bastard into a folk hero. There are moving coffee houses. The goose steals no fewer than two boa</span>
  <span id="freeText15934951331668137586" style="display:none">Everybody read this immediately. (Ignore the cover and don't bother reading any promo copy, because the marketing department fixated on the Macguffin and got it two-thirds wrong anyway.)<br /><br />Mosca, a smart, stubborn, and angry hick who totes a homicidal goose named Saracen, follows a con man named Eponymous Clent to the big city. Espionage, guild warfare, and murder ensue. They accidentally turn some poor bastard into a folk hero. There are moving coffee houses. The goose steals no fewer than two boats. <br /><br />This is shelved as a kid's book, but it doesn't read young. Actually, the quality of the prose is one of the best things about it -- it’s elegant and pointy and wonderful. <br /><br />But there’s so much more to like about it, too! The setting is grand, the history and the religion (no real gods, but about two hundred saints) are fantastic; the characters are solid and smudged and everyone is kind of a huge bastard. (Except The Cakes, who is a sweet-hearted and respectable girl and who only counts as a bastard in the technical sense.) Stabs of startling insight are just scattered around like tacks. Basically, it was an absolute joy to read at all times. I am now saving the rest of the author’s works for a rainy day.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15934951331668137586" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3651275315" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3651275315" />
    <a title="The Captain" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54489623-the-captain"><img alt="The Captain" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459976325p2/54489623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3651275315?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Captain" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Captain" href="/user/show/54489623-the-captain">The Captain</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54489623-the-captain?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3651275315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15173139984100646468">Ahoy there me mateys!  I was in a mood where I wasn't sure what I wanted to read.  Then I read Matey Nicky's review of this book where she said:<br/><blockquote>I have to admit that, primed by Untitled Goose Game, I was on Saracen’s side in all of this. In any given scene, at any given stopping point, my main concern was <em>where is Saracen???  </em>(People who watched me live-tweeting my binge of this book can attest to that. <em>Several</em> tweets demanding to know where the goose was.)  Part of the reason I was on Saracen’s </blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText15173139984100646468" style="display:none">Ahoy there me mateys!  I was in a mood where I wasn't sure what I wanted to read.  Then I read Matey Nicky's review of this book where she said:<br /><blockquote>I have to admit that, primed by Untitled Goose Game, I was on Saracen’s side in all of this. In any given scene, at any given stopping point, my main concern was <em>where is Saracen???  </em>(People who watched me live-tweeting my binge of this book can attest to that. <em>Several</em> tweets demanding to know where the goose was.)  Part of the reason I was on Saracen’s side is that things get a bit twisty. Who do you trust? By the last hundred pages, I only trusted Saracen.</blockquote><br />I have enjoyed this author's work in the past and the goose was the right incentive to immediately pick up this debut work of hers.  I loved it.<br /><br />This book is twisty and just so much fun.  It immediately captured me attention with the prologue where there is a discussion on what to name the new baby.  She was born on the name day of Goodman Palpitattle also known as  “He Who Keeps Flies out of Jams and Butter Churns.”  The midwife , Celery, is clearly concerned about the timing of her birth and the importance of names given her own.  But she is overruled and the baby gets named after the housefly - Mosca.<br /><br />Like always, the world building is just exquisite.  The plot follows poor Mosca as she tries to escape her horrible hamlet and just gets into more and more trouble.  Her problem?  She can <em>read </em>and reading is dangerous.  Whether it is the names of the gods or the lovely descriptions of the world or Mosca's opinions about what she sees, the word play in this book was delightful.  Like Eponymous Clem, the stranger that Mosca gets involved with.  Or this description of a path:<br /><blockquote>The path was a troublesome, fretful thing. It worried that it was missing a view of the opposite hills and insisted on climbing for a better look. Then it found the breeze uncommonly chill and ducked back among the trees. It suddenly thought it had forgotten something and doubled back, then realized that it hadn’t and turned about again. At last it struggled free of the pines, plumped itself down by the riverside, complained of its aching stones and refused to go any farther. A sensible, well-trodden track took over.</blockquote><br />Just lovely.  The plot is a bit convoluted at times but I didn't care because I loved the world and the characters.  I anxiously needed to know what happened next (and where the goose was!).  This book could be read as a standalone but the author did write a sequel six years later.  I am certainly going to be picking up a copy.  Arrr!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15173139984100646468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10714822552009604576" style="display:none">I loved this book. <div id="review_394759951" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/394759951" />
    <a title="Linna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3226530-linna"><img alt="Linna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330731364p2/3226530.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/394759951?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linna" href="/user/show/3226530-linna">Linna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3226530-linna?shelf=best-characters">best-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3226530-linna?shelf=maniacal-laughter-inducing">maniacal-laughter-inducing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3226530-linna?shelf=favorite-protagonists">favorite-protagonists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3226530-linna?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3226530-linna?shelf=impossible-to-put-down">impossible-to-put-down</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3226530-linna?shelf=highly-recommended">highly-recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3226530-linna?shelf=gorgeous-writing">gorgeous-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3226530-linna?shelf=overlooked-gems">overlooked-gems</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3226530-linna?shelf=surprisingly-good">surprisingly-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3226530-linna?shelf=oh-my-god-that-ending">oh-my-god-that-ending</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer394759951" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13580504767167432291">Where do I even start?<br/><br/>You'd think that after so many years of devouring books that I wouldn't be reduced to the speechless mess that I am right now, marveling at how <i>Fly by Night</i> manages to keep getting better with every page, how it keeps surprising me with a new wonderful way of wording something as it paints so many vivid pictures of its characters with a few deft strokes. <br/><br/>From the first few pages I was in love, and it's hard not to because here is a book that loves words just as much as you </span>
  <span id="freeText13580504767167432291" style="display:none">Where do I even start?<br /><br />You'd think that after so many years of devouring books that I wouldn't be reduced to the speechless mess that I am right now, marveling at how <i>Fly by Night</i> manages to keep getting better with every page, how it keeps surprising me with a new wonderful way of wording something as it paints so many vivid pictures of its characters with a few deft strokes. <br /><br />From the first few pages I was in love, and it's hard not to because here is a book that loves words just as much as you do, and brings out the power they have in a way that's nothing short of amazing. As it went on I only fell harder as the world really came to life with all its intricate details and god, that plot. There are so many different threads going on at once, but they're layered in a way that seems effortless. Small hints and details come back and the stakes keep rising as conspiracies, motives, schemes, and factions collide. It's wonderfully unpredictable, and a major reason for that is because the characters are always surprising me.<br /><br />The characters aren't merely likable, they're tricky and clever, angry and frightened but resilient and entertaining as hell. And that's just a few words for Mosca, our lead, who has 'the keen instincts of the unloved', and the first time she feels like someone wants her around, it was a feeling 'too strange and new to be thrown away lightly.' The fact that that someone is a con man of questionable character keeps things from getting sappy. <br /><br />I don't think I can describe the characters better than Hardinge can, so here's a few snippets.<br /><br /><blockquote>"When he smiled, his eyebrows rose into two neat chestnut crescents, as if they knew the world was destined to surprise them again and again, and were determined to believe in pleasant surprises."<br /><br />"Sometimes fear made you angry. Perhaps after years anger cooled, like a sword taken from the forge. Perhaps in the end you were left with something very cold and very sharp."<br /><br />"But in the name of the most holy, Mosca, of all the people you could have taken up with, why Eponymous Clent?"<br /><i>Because I’d been hoarding words for years, buying them from pedlars and carving them secretly on to bits of bark so I wouldn’t forget them, and then he turned up using words like ‘epiphany’ and ‘amaranth’. Because I heard him talking in the marketplace, laying out sentences like a merchant rolling out rich silks. Because he made words and ideas dance like flames and something that was damp and dying came alive in my mind, the way it hadn’t since they burned my father’s books. Because he walked into Chough with stories from exciting places tangled around him like maypole streamers . . .</i><br />Mosca shrugged.<br />"He’s got a way with words."</blockquote><br /><br />I guess I shouldn't be surprised that a book so dedicated to the love of reading and words captivated me because I'm a sucker for that kind of thing. But this book doesn't try to play off those feelings, it takes them and makes the most of all the potential and power that words can have. It's brimming with ideas, rich world-building, lovely moments, and whenever I think about it I can't help smiling. I think I forgot to mention that it's hilarious too. Just.... read this book, stat.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13580504767167432291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1325930293" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1325930293" />
    <a title="Jeanette" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11029945-jeanette"><img alt="Jeanette" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442988435p2/11029945.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1325930293?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeanette" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeanette" href="/user/show/11029945-jeanette">Jeanette</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330418263" href="/book/show/205034.Fly_by_Night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11029945-jeanette?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11029945-jeanette?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11029945-jeanette?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11029945-jeanette?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11029945-jeanette?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1325930293" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11851538162275406394">I absolutely loved Frances Hardinge's <i>A Face Like Glass</i> so I had high expectations of <i>Fly by Night</i>. Perhaps that was a little unfair as <i>Fly by Night</i> is Hardinge's debut novel (published in 2005). <br/><br/>Twelve year old Mosca Mye is named after the common housefly by her erudite, eccentric, book-loving, historian and philosopher father Quillam Mye. After his death, Quillam Mye's books and histories are burnt by the frightened villages in the rain soaked village of Clough. Eventually word-hungry Mosca is</span>
  <span id="freeText11851538162275406394" style="display:none">I absolutely loved Frances Hardinge's <i>A Face Like Glass</i> so I had high expectations of <i>Fly by Night</i>. Perhaps that was a little unfair as <i>Fly by Night</i> is Hardinge's debut novel (published in 2005). <br /><br />Twelve year old Mosca Mye is named after the common housefly by her erudite, eccentric, book-loving, historian and philosopher father Quillam Mye. After his death, Quillam Mye's books and histories are burnt by the frightened villages in the rain soaked village of Clough. Eventually word-hungry Mosca is able to escape the un-tender 'care' of her aunt and uncle with her only friend, the goose Saracen, and the wordsmith, Eponymous Clent, of dubious character and motivations despite his flowery prose. They end up in the city of Mandelion and find themselves in the thick of a plot to overthrow the city, a guild war between the locksmiths and stationers and all kinds of chaos and mayhem. Mosca needs to find where her heart truly lies, and the path to freedom and knowledge.<br /><br />There is much to like in this baroque book based on Victorian England, with a good dash of the aftermath of French Reign of Terror mixed in. Hardinge conjures up unique and memorial characters worthy of Dickens, a complex plot, some quirky and occasionally evocative description and a convoluted and vivid world with the finesse reminiscent of <i>A Face Like Glass</i>. The book uses omniscient point of view though it largely from Mosca's perspective. While it took me over half the book to begin to warm to Mosca as character, I do like the human touches in the growing friendship between Mosca and Clent or Mosca and the Cakes. The plot had satisfying layers, even if a little predictable for the thinking reader. <br /><br />I think not connecting with Mosca at first made this book less compelling reading than <i>A Face Like Glass</i> but what I was particularly disappointed in was the cardboard cut out stereotypes of the motivations of the antagonists, especially the birdcatcher villain, which is clearly pushing the author's own (non)faith position. It seems to me that in 20th century - or most other centuries for that matter - that people who lack of belief in one God have been as guilty of programs and terror (from Stalin to Mao to Pol Pot), while on the other hand, 18th century deists and theists were just as (or more) likely to be building hospitals, schools or be involved in social reform for workers, the poor, women, children, prisoners and/or slaves, supporting freedom of speech and democracy - as inciting homicidal mayhem. <br /><br />While Mosca is a very young protagonist, the complexity of prose and plot is probably more Young Adult in tone. A book worth reading. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11851538162275406394" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
