    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_151021610" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151021610" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4063913-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351396026p2/4063913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151021610?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/4063913-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4063913-beth?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151021610" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16341076509967438346">This book reads like a mashup of a few other young YA novels to me, meaning it doesn't feel very original, and the plot is a bit ludicrous. The writing, though, is so original and clever and the kingdom's history so well laid out and explained that combined they prevent any melodrama.<br/><br/>First, the writing: <i>Fly by Night</i> flows smoothly, yes, but it also showcases a uniquely twelve-year-old experience. Hardinge removes her perspective so completely from the novel that she manages to create characteriz</span>
  <span id="freeText16341076509967438346" style="display:none">This book reads like a mashup of a few other young YA novels to me, meaning it doesn't feel very original, and the plot is a bit ludicrous. The writing, though, is so original and clever and the kingdom's history so well laid out and explained that combined they prevent any melodrama.<br /><br />First, the writing: <i>Fly by Night</i> flows smoothly, yes, but it also showcases a uniquely twelve-year-old experience. Hardinge removes her perspective so completely from the novel that she manages to create characterization through word choice. The novel never lets you forget, through its very words, that this is its protagonist's story. This is seen most cleverly through use of metaphor and simile, which themselves depict Mosca's age and range of experience:<br /><blockquote>The jokes they exchanged were like clods of earth thrown at the face, mean good-humoredly - but meant to bruise as well.<br /><br />...Mosca felt less alone. It was a strange and shiny new feeling, and she decided not to think about it too hard, in case she wore the paint off it.</blockquote><br />The kingdom's history is wonderfully done as well, rich in metaphor and completely believable. It evokes the French Revolution with its descriptions of terror and wanton death, tyranny and rebels. Some of the novel's strongest writing describes the evolution of the kingdom's religion.<br /><blockquote>Afterward it was hard to be sure exactly when the sublime light had dazzled their minds and driven them mad, since they went insane with such calm and dignity that nobody noticed.</blockquote><br />The ways Hardinge uses words and multiple meanings to create <i>layers</i> is nothing short of brilliance. One can read the book for the writing alone.<br /><br />An added benefit, though, is the book's description of the discovery of truth and the ways it can be hindered and spread. The discovery of the importance of both freedom of speech and of the press. The discovery that people are never what they seem and that they can be more complex than ever imagined. That not even smart twelve-year-olds can foresee everything or always be correct. All this in a highly entertaining, potentially ridiculous but ultimately wonderful story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16341076509967438346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16317047" />
    <a title="Eshusdaughter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/742623-eshusdaughter"><img alt="Eshusdaughter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505110197p2/742623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16317047?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eshusdaughter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eshusdaughter" href="/user/show/742623-eshusdaughter">Eshusdaughter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/742623-eshusdaughter?shelf=read-in-2008">read-in-2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/742623-eshusdaughter?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/742623-eshusdaughter?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16317047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9387322192475745019">Mosca Mye and her goose Saracen are certainly an odd couple of heros, but charming ones none the less. The underlying story is a good one with lots of twists and turns that satisfy as well as suprise. <br/><br/>This book receives only three stars, however, for several reasons. First, the author is a little too enamored of simile and comparison. There are some really great similes in this book but also some humongous clankers. Many of the comparison's the author makes just don't fit or make sense. There is</span>
  <span id="freeText9387322192475745019" style="display:none">Mosca Mye and her goose Saracen are certainly an odd couple of heros, but charming ones none the less. The underlying story is a good one with lots of twists and turns that satisfy as well as suprise. <br /><br />This book receives only three stars, however, for several reasons. First, the author is a little too enamored of simile and comparison. There are some really great similes in this book but also some humongous clankers. Many of the comparison's the author makes just don't fit or make sense. There is also a tendency to focus on minutia too much and over-description. Perhaps because of those tendencies, the book is a lot longer than it should be and it begins to lose a bit of the enchantment after awhile. I like a good long book, when the story warrants it, I don't feel that was the case here and there were clear areas that could and should have been trimmed. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9387322192475745019" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8143131693514640897">i wholly sympathized with Mosca's love of words and appreciated that Hardinge used such wonderfully descriptive language. "The papery sound of rain" is fantastically perfect! I also like that she inverted the usual fantasy triangle: instead of introducing many characters who are doing different things and then they converge, the characters in this one all meet in the beginning, touch again and then the action is spread out. Very nice</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2673539263" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2673539263" />
    <a title="Giulia (moonrise.bookdom)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59472542-giulia-moonrise-bookdom"><img alt="Giulia (moonrise.bookdom)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547231347p2/59472542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2673539263?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giulia (moonrise.bookdom)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giulia (moonrise.bookdom)" href="/user/show/59472542-giulia-moonrise-bookdom">Giulia (moonrise.bookdom)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/39781771-fly-by-night">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2673539263" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13539815763183125180">*4.5/5 stars.<br/><br/>Being the first book published by Hardinge, I didn't set my expectations too high and I though I would find something less accomplished than her most recent books. Boy I was wrong!<br/><br/>Fly by Night is set in a fantastic kingdom loosely inspired by XVIII England, the "fragmented realm". The protagonist is Mosca Mye, a twelve-year-old orphan girl who's had enough of living with her unloving uncle and aunt in a little village where books are banned. So she burns down her relatives' mill and</span>
  <span id="freeText13539815763183125180" style="display:none">*4.5/5 stars.<br /><br />Being the first book published by Hardinge, I didn't set my expectations too high and I though I would find something less accomplished than her most recent books. Boy I was wrong!<br /><br />Fly by Night is set in a fantastic kingdom loosely inspired by XVIII England, the "fragmented realm". The protagonist is Mosca Mye, a twelve-year-old orphan girl who's had enough of living with her unloving uncle and aunt in a little village where books are banned. So she burns down her relatives' mill and leaves for good with her goose Saracen and a questionable man named Eponymous Clent who lies and tricks people using a flamboyant rethoric. The pair of them soon reaches the city of Mandelion, and Mosca will find herself in the middle of intricate political schemes and religious factions.<br /><br />The world-building is rich and detailed but also immediate to dive in, one as only Hardinge can craft. Mosca is a great protagonist, and she goes through an amazing and realistic growth during her adventures. I had a great time reading this book, I loved the clever storylines that weave adventure, numerous but always credible twists, and ponderings about power, religion, censorship, the right for everyone to search for their own truth. I just couldn't have enough of running around Mandelion.<br /><br />It's really difficult to express all the things that one can find in a Frances Hardinge book while still having a fun time reading. Fly by Nights is definitely one of my favourite ones now and I think it would be a great starting point for everyone to discover this brilliant author!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13539815763183125180" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1951290654" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1951290654" />
    <a title="Stefan Bachmann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7045138-stefan-bachmann"><img alt="Stefan Bachmann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541686398p2/7045138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1951290654?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stefan Bachmann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stefan Bachmann" href="/user/show/7045138-stefan-bachmann">Stefan Bachmann</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7045138-stefan-bachmann?shelf=audible">audible</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1951290654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17904959300483535707">Whew! This is for readers who love reading for the actual words: the way they sound and fit together, paint pictures, pile up to form the layers of a fictional world. Lots of readers like the glass-pane method, where the writing is mostly invisible in service of the story, but I love a book that revels in the actual *sentences*. This is that sort of book. It's all about words. It's about how they shape perceptions and history, the way writing can seed rebellion, be lovely or terrible and dangero</span>
  <span id="freeText17904959300483535707" style="display:none">Whew! This is for readers who love reading for the actual words: the way they sound and fit together, paint pictures, pile up to form the layers of a fictional world. Lots of readers like the glass-pane method, where the writing is mostly invisible in service of the story, but I love a book that revels in the actual *sentences*. This is that sort of book. It's all about words. It's about how they shape perceptions and history, the way writing can seed rebellion, be lovely or terrible and dangerous. The book is just infused with an admiration for language, and I liked how every aspect of the book - from the super political plot to the fancy, loopy prose to the characters and their motivations - illustrates its points. (The naming practices in this book are some of my favourite ever: Eponymous Clent, Lady Tamarind Avourlace, Mabwick Toke, Hopewood Pertellis. So good.) <br /><br />This isn't a fashionably fast-paced or straightforward sort of MG, and there's not a lot of fantastical elements or wish-fulfilment, but I liked it a lot. Am on a quest to read all of Frances Hardinge's stuff now just for those delicious descriptions.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17904959300483535707" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wSEZWb4csZ1I4tHKVX3hxUEaXhqfTMnSC49if1nZWYqPSB+8TkUFqDz1ML4o7OAbL89Snz5PmMl1DEVyhpEwYQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8N1d03yDU4MAx7eLpXkkZI4sYY/ZLxJk95ZNOLJb8Yi+tFs2jNrntnTQVv/Y6CW64PltCngsQ3+JFWo1bROYYw==')})
  }
